< review>
I'm sorry to say that if I could I would give this hospital no stars. A while back I stayed at this hospital because I was going through things in my life and I needed help that is all. I was struggling and I needed someone to talk things through with but unfortunately this was not the case. When I first arrived at this hospital they ask me for a urine sample and to check my body to count my scars and cuts and to make sure I didn't have anything on me, which is understandable. The lady who viewed me took me into a room and asked me if I was religious and if I was, what religion. i proceeded to tell her I am Christian, I was just going through things and needed extra help to work things out. She told me I was going to hell for putting my family in this position and that I should think really hard about what I had done to them...ARE you kidding me?? first off I was a minor at the time and second how dare you. The staff was extremely disrespectful... I saw the psychiatrist twice. Once when I got there and and right before I was about to leave less than five minutes both times. They drew my blood and when I asked why they didn't give me an answer. the rooms were disgusting... my roommate peed on the floor and no one came to clean it.. it sat on the floor for at least a few hours. The pictures they provide are not accurate.. there are paintings on the windows to so you cannot see outside in any windows.. there is writing on the walls in the rooms...I have my nose pierced and I had it done two years before I came to this hospital and I have never had a problem with it, however coming here I got a bad infection in my nose... Phone time is REALLY limited there were days were I didn't get to talk to my mom. Once my dad came to visit and there was a vending machine there and he gave the staff money to give to me. when he left he called making sure I got the money they told him they gave it to me. when I finally talked to him on the phone he asked me if I got any money I told him I didn't. This hospital did not help and I would not recommend to anyone. the only thing positive that came out of this hospital was sparking my interest and motivation to go into the medical field to make sure no one has to go through what I did.<//review>

I'm a 17 year old boy was here for a total of 6 days for saying stupid, threatening things online, thus leading to the common-sense conclusion that I am mentally ill. If anyone was in with me during my time (10/27-11/1), I was the short skinny Asian dude with the ponytail who didn't talk or hang out with the other boys much. I honestly thought this hospital was decent though, it isn't as bad as other former patients are saying it is. I got to make new friends for life, learn valuable life lessons, and the staff are not bad at all unless you're a complete idiot. Food is definitely better than the food my school, and beds are serviceable. If you're well behaved, take care of yourself, and take medication they give you,  the psychiatrist there should be letting you out sooner than later. Never once when I was in here did I ever have thoughts of escaping or even wanting to go home. This will definitely be an experience in my life I never forget.</Review>

Having had extensive non helpful treatment for severe trauma I discovered Del Amo"s trauma unit. I was amazed at how different this unit is from average psychiatric units. There knowledge of trauma ability to give you the skills and knowledge to learn to life beyond the traumas effects is remarkable. The staff is kind, respectful, and understanding. The work that is done there can be intense , but it is healing and sacred. I can't say enough positive things about this unit and hospital.I received help that I had never received before. My life is going well now and I am deeply grateful to the staff and program. It is definitely worth the ten hour drive each way to get there and back. I would go back to this unit in a minute if I ever needed to.  The staff is so caring. I can't recommend this unit and its program enough.<//text>

< text>
My review is a bit long overdue but I felt the need to still submit a review in hopes to help ease the minds of mothers like myself who happen to come across this experience which I personally could compare to a nightmare.
My 12 year old son was brought to Del Amo after being placed on a 72 hr hold and after seeing all these horrible reviews my mother instinct kicked in. I couldn't bare the newly expressed feeling of my 12 year old who to me seemed normal, let alone be okay with him being transferred to such a "horrible" facility.
It is true we have no say where our kids get transferred to after being placed on a 72 hr hold and I was very upset that I was not told that after being transported in the ambulance and taken into the facility through the back door, the nurse that opened the door didn't notify me that I would not be able to see my son anymore. All she told me was that I couldn't go in through the back and that i had to go through the front lobby. If I would have known I wasn't going to be able to see my son until the following day I would have hugged and kissed him goodbye but ofcourse, I found that out after I had been sent to the lobby. I was able to speak to him through the phone when I called the unit he was in.
Aside from that for a psychiatric facility, which some people in previous reviews seem to forget , they do their job and are helpful as much as they could be.
My son was the oldest for his unit and they were patient enough to answer my every annoying question even when calling as early as 6AM. I always made sure to take down the names of every person I spoke to. When the kids wouldn't pick up the payphone, I would call the nurses station and they'd explain that the kids were in group.
My son didn't really complain, he did say he wanted to go home and that he didn't want to be there but him knowing how overprotective I am over him he didn't complain. He just wanted to come home. Again he was placed on a 72-hr hold so to my understanding he was just gonna be monitored to make sure he wasn't a threat to himself or others. I did expect for him to speak to the psychiatrist for longer than he did but I also understand my son was not his patient and that the Dr was there to evaluate and help make a recommendation as far as treatment.
Upon leaving the place we were set up with a follow up appointment with my son's therapist and given a copy of the documents that pertained to my son.
Unfortunately, being sent to places like these aren't planned but they do their job.
As far as the stars goes for this review, I choose one star cause  I need to give it stars because in my honest opinion you can't really rate a psychiatric hospital with stars... lol
Hope this review helps scared, first time(and last, I hope) mothers like myself keep an open mind.< /text>

< Review>
This is NOT the place for your child or loved one to go! If you or your child needs to be admitted somewhere, try UCLA, or BHC. Both are a million times better. IF you're looking for residential treatment (which I highly recommend) Evolve is an incredible place to look into. Lastly, if you are looking for PHP, or IOP, Engage is another beautiful program where the staff genuinely cares about you. I just graduated a week or two ago, and I can't thank them enough. I wish you the best of luck! Don't be fooled by the pretty pictures they've falsely advertised with.

If you're still not convinced this is a little of what happened while I was there:

I was admitted here September 19th 2016. I was having serious suicidal ideation and I needed to go someplace where I would be safe. When I was admitted I had had no history of past hospital stays and I was already scared of my thoughts and terrified to stay away from my family. When I got there, they sat me and my father down in a nice and clean room to take down our info and admit me. Then they took me through a big metal door and had me say goodbye to my father. Once we were through that door there was a HUGE contrast. It was dirty, and dimly lit. it was something out of a horror movie. They took my vitals, my things, and then gave me a plastic pillow thing, a thin yellow blanket and a sheet, and sent me to a room with three other girls (already asleep).

The conditions were just as bad all through the rest of the days I was there. (The food was hospital food so you know it isn't really the best, but that wasn't an issue really.) The staff was cruel. They treated everyone like criminals. They would make everyone come into a sort of "cafeteria" area, and sit and shut up while some unqualified old man handed out worksheets we had to complete. Then they would lock us in our rooms for two or three hours. (This was a cycle that just repeated itself over and over again until it was time for bed.)

"Booty-Juice" is a term I learned here. It means that if you get too rambunctious, they will hold you down, take your pants off, and stick a shot in your ass to knock you out. It was done quite often.

The girls I stayed with were my saving grace. They were the only kind people there. Although there were many psychotic breakdowns with screaming threats of murder and not being able to control the violent voices in one's head (which is something that they can't help themselves).

At the end of the week, I was a different person. A little piece of me died there, and I can never get it back.
AGAIN: If you or your child needs to be admitted somewhere, try UCLA, or BHC. Both are a million times better. IF you're looking for residential treatment (which I highly recommend) Evolve is an incredible place to look into. Lastly, if you are looking for PHP, or IOP, Engage is another beautiful program where the staff genuinely cares about you. I just graduated a week or two ago, and I can't thank them enough. I wish you the best of luck! Don't be fooled by the pretty pictures they've falsely advertised with.</Review>

This place is straight out of a HORROR film. I went in with anxiety and depression with mild suicidal ideation. I ended up with PTSD after this place. They lied in my paperwork and said I attempted suicide. From the moment I stepped in there, they said I would be there 5-6 days before they even did an evaluation (can I even call it an evaluation? It was 3 Q's).

With the help of my parents, and absolute PERSISTENCE, calling them out on broken laws, I managed to get out in 3 days. Others were not so lucky.

If you know someone in there, the most important thing they can do is put on an act. Act like you are happy, attend all the groups, go to all meals, tell the psychiatrist you are doing great and are looking forward to getting back into the routine of things at home, and have a smile on at all times. You cannot trust anyone. If you tell any staff member that you are anxious, depressed etc you will likely get on a 14 day hold. They will do everything they can to get your insurance money. Call them nonstop even when they stall or don't help. Be pushy but don't yell. Same for the patient, do everything you can to act nice to the staff even when some are verbally abusive. If you make them mad they will increase your hold.

They threw everyone together in the acute psychiatric ward: men and women of all ages, people detoxing from heroin/meth/alcohol, schizophrenia, depression, hallucinations, violence toward others. People threatened to kill me, had bloodied faces and received no medical attention, and one man broke out screaming and threatening everyone and the staff didn't have anywhere safe for us to go.

It's 4 months after and I was recently diagnosed with PTSD. I still have nightmares, flashbacks, and am really shaky most of the time.

If you know someone in there right now, know that I say a prayer every night for the people who are currently in there</Review>

<Review>This is the first time I have ever actually been inspired to follow through in writing a negative review for anyone. The only reason this pharmacy should even have a star at all is that it provides life saving medicine to people who need it, which is only because it is in fact a pharmacy. I have  been using the CVS pharmacy on 41st Ave. for about 4 years beginning with the birth of my second child. It was the natural choice as it was the only pharmacy nearby with a drive through. It is hard enough being sick, let alone dragging in 2 small children along with you. I have to say the drive through window (despite it's colossally slow wait times) remains the most positive thing about the service  of this pharmacy. Think about that: a physical structure being the best thing about a place where thousands of people come. So, why do I say this? For all the years I've been coming, I have been frustrated by incredibly long wait times whether inside or at the drive through, prescriptions not being ready even after having received text messages that they are, and then having to wait an additional 30-45 minutes for them to get those prescriptions ready, long  wait times for prescriptions to be ready after coming from the doctor's office, and waiting on hold for up to 45 minutes on one occasion to speak to someone in the department. The common complaint I have seems to be wait time. Which is what I kind of expect from a pharmacy to some degree, which is why that drive through window and the potential that I might need it when picking up a prescription has kept me coming back. Until today.
Last night I was prescribed something that I needed to start ASAP and CVS was closed so it got sent to the Walgreens on Freedom. I got to the Walgreens only to discover that they were out of both the medications I needed. Fine, it happens. They told me that I needed to ask my pharmacy to call them to transfer the prescription over to them. I got to CVS first thing this morning (to avoid the dreaded wait time), and was able to speak with someone pretty quickly (a nice change). They said it would be 15-20 minutes for the prescription to be ready ( which honestly does feel much longer - not their fault- with two kids in the car and a full blown case of Influenza A) and one of the medications was. The other wasn't showing up, so I told them what the pharmacist at Walgreens said. The tech at CVS said it would take a bit but they would call when it was ready. No problem. So when I get the call from the pharmacist she says that she called the Walgreens and was on hold for 12 minutes and no one answered so it might be faster for me to ask them to transfer it. I explained that I was there in person last night and asked them to transfer it and that I was clearly instructed that the pharmacy needed to call. Now, I have to admit that my years of frustration may have emerged a bit. She continued on to say it might be faster if I call ( did she not hear me?) To which I told her, no it would not be and that considering the hours I have collectively waited for things from them, couldn't they call back try again. Wasn't it part of what they do at the pharmacy? To which she replied she could not sit and wait on hold for a pharmacist for all that time. To which I replied that I know all about waiting on hold for pharmacists considering I've been using theirs for years. And could I please speak with their manager? Her response was that she would not continue to be verbally abused and hung up on me.
I guess I need to figure something else out for my prescription? I get that whoever I was talking to was not responsible for all of my collective frustration, and that if she was waiting on hold it would be taking her away from other customers who would then be frustrated by having to wait. I also realized that I may be overly agitated as a result of having a fever and feeling generally miserable. My frustrations have spanned years and are countless. Being hung up on is the final straw.< /Review>< user_name>
